අෙප් නීල් ඉද්දවල මහත්මයාත් ඒ වාෙග්ම නිරහංකාර ෙබොෙහොම පියශීලි ෙකෙනක්. හැම තිස්ෙසේම හිනා ෙවලා ඉන්න තුන් ෙදනකු හැටියට තමයි අපි ඔබතුමන්ලා දකින්ෙන්. එතුමාත් නිෙයෝජ්‍ය මහ ෙල්කම් තනතුරට පත් වී තිෙබනවා. ඔබතුමාටත් ෙම් ගමන ඉහළට ගිහිල්ලා ෙම් උත්තරීතර සභාව ෙශෝභාවත් කරන්නට භාග්‍ය ලැෙබන්න කියලා පාර්ථනා කරනවා.

ධම්මික කිතුල්ෙගොඩ මැතිතුමනි, ඔබතුමාට ඥාතිත්වයක් තිෙබන පුද්ගලයකු හැටියටත්, ඔබතුමාෙග් ගති පැවතුම් අගය කරන පුද්ගලයකු හැටියටත් ඔබතුමාට සුබ පතමින් මෙග් වචන ස්වල්පය අවසන් කරනවා.

නිෙයෝජ්‍ය කාරක සභාපතිතුමා (குᾨக்களின் பிரதித் தவிசாளர் அவர்கள்) (Mr. Deputy Chairman of Committees) The next speaker is the Hon. Alhaj A.H.M. Azwer. Please try to finish your speech within five minutes.

[5.11 p.m.] ගරු අල්හාජ් ඒ.එච්.එම්. අස්වර් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு அல்ஹாஜ் ஏ.எச்.எம். அஸ்வர்) (The Hon. Alhaj A.H.M. Azwer) Mr. Deputy Chairman of Committees, let me initially quote two great authorities on Parliament in order to illustrate the greatness, the importance and the significance of the post of Secretary-General of Parliament.

On page 197 of the "Erskine May’s Treatise on The Law, Privileges, Proceedings and Usage of Parliament”, it is stated, I quote:

“Principal Permanent Officers of the Commons - Clerk of the House.” We mean, the Secretary-General of Parliament. It is further stated, I quote:

“The Clerk of the House is the chief permanent officer of the House of Commons. He is appointed by the Crown, ...”

Here, it is His Excellency the President.

“...for life, ...” But, you are appointed for a peried.

“... by letters patent, in which he is styled ‘Under Clerk of the Parliaments...to attend upon the Commons’.

The Clerk has the custody of all records or other documents, and is responsible for the conduct of the business of the House in the offices within his department. He assists the Speaker and advises Members in regard to questions of order

and the proceedings of the House. He is the Corporate Officer of the House and holds the appointments of Accounting Officer for the House of Commons and Chairman of the Board of Management.”

Then, Sir, let us take another example from our close neighbour, India. I quote from the book “Practice and Procedure of Parliament” written by M.N. Kaul and S.L. Shakdher and edited by G.C. Malhotra. It states, I quote:

“The position of the Secretary-General of the Lok Sabha…”

It is equivalent to Parliament here.

“…is a most unusual one; one might almost say that it is unique.”

This position of the Secretary-General is also unique.

“ He is expected to know everything that is to be known about everything that has any reference to the Lok Sabha and its business, whether it relates to some rather abstruse constitutional point or the proper precedence that should be followed

in certain given circumstances; whatever the problem, members expect immediate and authoritative advice from him. In fact, the efficient and proper working of the House depends largely on the Secretary-General.” Then, again it states, I quote:

“No two persons are more closely associated than the Speaker and the Secretary-General. A relationship of utmost confidence in each other exists between them. The Secretary-General may be very competent; he may also be in the midst of politics, yet by training he is not a politician. He, therefore, lacks something which is filled in by the Speaker.”

So, Sir, it is a unique position that Mr. Dhammika Kitulgoda occupied and today we find him seated in his usual chair and we are very happy that he has entered the House once more. He is elegantly seated.

The period Mr. Dhammika Kitulgoda enjoyed most in his career was the 20 years he spent in the judiciary. I would go back to that. He became the youngest-ever Magistrate in Sri Lanka at 28 and rose up to be the Secretary of the Judicial Service Commission. I should record this in English because about 1,000 members of the Commonwealth Parliaments will be assembling here in September. He did the groundwork and they must know who he really is.

He was one judge who was able to bring down the workload in every station he worked. In certain stations, he saw to it that all the trial cases on the trial roll were disposed of before he was transferred out. He was able to dispose of the work mainly by effecting settlements by

119 120

[ගරු ගයන්ත කරුණාතිලක මහතා]

2012 ෙපබරවාරි 22

having a dialogue with the parties in the case. This way, heavily- contested civil cases like partitions and land cases which were 30 - 40 years old were concluded to the satisfaction of all parties concerned. Therefore, some Members of the Bar referred to him as the Samadana Vinishchakara. It is not the JP that we used to refer to. It really means, Samadana Vinishchakara – one who metes out justice in the proper way.

When he came back to Parliament, there were many pending matters and fundamental rights cases in litigation with regard to the Parliament staff and he was able to intervene and settle them all.

Then, Sir, let me state what he has done for the benefit of the Parliament staff. A 30 per cent allowance was given to them and the Sitting Allowance was increased without any discrimination to the minor employees. Then, there were promotions for the minor grades and he established a category of Junior Clerks, enabling the minor staff to advance in their career. An unprecedented number of Parliament employees were given foreign exposure and even from the minor grades, people were sent on study tours. If not for Mr. Dhammika Kitulgoda, the Buddhist Society in Parliament would never have been a reality.

At this point, Sir, I should recall the services of Mr. Bandula Abeysekara who was a power of strength to the Secretary Genaral in this Service.

නිෙයෝජ්‍ය කාරක සභාපතිතුමා (குᾨக்களின் பிரதித் தவிசாளர் அவர்கள்) (Mr. Deputy Chairman of Committees) Hon. Member, please wind up now. ගරු අල්හාජ් ඒ.එච්.එම්. අස්වර් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு அல்ஹாஜ் ஏ.எச்.எம். அஸ்வர்) (The Hon. Alhaj A.H.M. Azwer) Let me continue, Sir, because I am taking the time of the Hon. (Ven.) Ellawala Medhananda Thero also.

නිෙයෝජ්‍ය කාරක සභාපතිතුමා (குᾨக்களின் பிரதித் தவிசாளர் அவர்கள்) (Mr. Deputy Chairman of Committees) There are a lot of speakers from the Government side. ගරු අල්හාජ් ඒ.එච්.එම්. අස්වර් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு அல்ஹாஜ் ஏ.எச்.எம். அஸ்வர்) (The Hon. Alhaj A.H.M. Azwer) Sir, this is the last chance. I am also a Member of the Chairman’s Panel. Let me have another five minutes.

නිෙයෝජ්‍ය කාරක සභාපතිතුමා (குᾨக்களின் பிரதித் தவிசாளர் அவர்கள்) (Mr. Deputy Chairman of Committees) No, I cannot give you more time.

ගරු අල්හාජ් ඒ.එච්.එම්. අස්වර් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு அல்ஹாஜ் ஏ.எச்.எம். அஸ்வர்) (The Hon. Alhaj A.H.M. Azwer) He supported multi-religious activities in Parliament such as Ifthar, Christmas Carols, Lakshmi Pooja and Saraswathi Pooja. During the time of Ifthar - breaking of fast - he was very helpful to all the Muslim Members of Parliament and the members of the staff.

The Anuradhapura Circuit Bungalow, which is going to be a reality within the next month or two was his brainchild. It is a pity that it could not be completed before his retirement. He was able to find the funding to give scholarships to the children of the Parliamentary staff allowing the Parliamentary Staff Union to generate an income by the sale of accumulated waste paper in Parliament. After he relinquished duties for the first time as the Secretary-General of Parliament and went to the Constitutional Council, the Parliamentary Staff Union saw it fit to name the Fund after him and they called it the “Dhammika Kitulgoda Scholarship Fund”.

He provided transport facilities for Muslims to attend the Mosque on Fridays. I thank him for that on behalf of all the Muslims in Parliament. The children of the staff of Parliament were given employment in the minor grades in Parliament. Sir, I would like to table* the rest of my speech to be included in the Hansard because this is very important and concerns the Secretary-General of Parliament.

But, before I conclude, I have a duty to welcome our present Secretary-General of Parliament, Mr. Waruna Bandara Dhammika Dasanayake, who is a gleaming and a lovable personality. Then, Sir, I would also like to welcome our Deputy Secretary-General Mr. Wijayasundara Mudiyanselage Neil Parakrama Iddawala. I must also welcome Mr. C. Kuruppu who became the Librarian of this Parliament during the time of Mr. Kitulgoda. He was very helpful to you and all of us. Then, there are also certain demands put forward by the others. I would only ask that those matters be attended to.

Sir, I do not know whether it is a coincidence or not; we must ask from their parents. Dhammika -ධම්මික- has a

Dhammika - ධම්මිකා- who is his beloved wife. He has two children, Ama and Uma. He attended Royal College. All of them form a lawyers’ quartet in their home! I would only like to give this advice to his children: imbibe the noble qualities and follow the footsteps of your dad and not be found wanting in your career.

Sir, you are a Tamil gentleman in the Chair. May I quote from "Thirukkural" and finish off to illustrate his sterling qualities.
